class="a-spacing-small">Most Helpful Customer Reviews</h3> <div id="revMHRL" class="a-section">                            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R3JTPGYUY4P51V" class="a-section"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">21 of 21 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="3.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R3JTPGYUY4P51V/ref=cm_cr_dp_title?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00066FH60&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-3"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R3JTPGYUY4P51V/ref=cm_cr_dp_title?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00066FH60&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">Not a lot of other choices out there</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A36IITL6Y3E5BW/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp" class="noTextDecoration">listenswithwolves</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on November 4, 2008</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R3JTPGYUY4P51V" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-secondary">Color Name: Black<i class="a-icon a-icon-text-separator"></i></span><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   I bought this stand for my home gym. It was the only one I could find at<br>a decent price that was also tall enough to be seen over my elliptical<br>trainer. It is a very solidly made stand, but not very well designed.<br><br>1st drawback: Nearly the entire thing is put together with tiny set<br>screws (a dozen in all) that you must tighten with a tiny allen wrench.<br>This makes height adjustments quite a pain. Peerless really should have<br>at least put a thumb screw at the height adjustment pipe. To workaround<br>this, I found an adjustable hose clamp with a built in plastic<br>thumbscrew at the 99cent store, and it works great.<br><br>2nd drawback: There is no up/down angle adjustment where the tv is<br>mounted, so it must always stay basically flat perpendicular to the<br>floor. Adding this feature would probably have added somewhat to the<br>price, but I would have gladly paid for it.<br><br>Other than these two issues, this is a solid and pretty nice-looking<br>stand which can also hide your cables pretty well. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R3JTPGYUY4P51V/ref=cm_cr_dp_cmt?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00066FH5Q&nodeID=172282&store=electronics#wasThisHelpful">Comment</a> <i class="a-icon a-icon-text-separator"></i> Helmuth</a>   </span> <span class="a-declarative" data-action="cr-popup" data-cr-popup="{&quot;width&quot;:340,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;AmazonHelp&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:340}" style="display:inline;"></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on February 16, 2012</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R8G99662HPIO9" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-secondary">Color Name: Silver<i class="a-icon a-icon-text-separator"></i></span><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   Bought this stand for mounting a 26" LCD television high enough to see it on the exercise bike in the basement workout room. It works great, and would be fine for a treadmill or other equipment. It is very well made and very easy to assemble with clear instructions. The price seemed high to me until I received it - the materials and machining are top quality. Before you buy it, though, be sure that your TV has a VESA 75 or 100 mounting pattern (hole spacing for the mounting plate screws). The LG televisions on Amazon list the VESA mounting patterns in the PDF spec sheet; for other manufacturers you may have download a product manual on the manufacturer's website and go to the wall mounting section for this info. Most but not all  TV's under 30" use VESA 75 or 100. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" It will easily mount a TV/Monitor up to roughly 28" (as long as the VESA is 100x100), without any extra purchases or equipment.  If you want to knock it down, you can.....its not the heaviest thing in the world. Its as if the manufacturer never actually fully tested their design.  I contacted the manufacturer and asked them to recommend a VGA cable for use. The responded with the following:<br><br>"Thank you for contacting Peerless Industries.  I contacted our engineering team and after testing with the cables, it has been found that the VGA cable will not work with this.  The tubing is not large enough to accommodate the plug."<br><br>So I would only recommend this product if you plan on having your vga cable exposed. </div>  </div>             <a class="a-link-normal M. Fleming</a>   </span> <span class="a-declarative" data-action="cr-popup" data-cr-popup="{&quot;width&quot;:340,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;AmazonHelp&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:340}" style="display:inline;"></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on September 6, 2011</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R1772EKMG28U94" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-secondary">Color Name: Black<i class="a-icon a-icon-text-separator"></i></span><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   I really wanted to like this item -- it was for a dorm room that didn't allow a wall mount. We mounted a 32" tv that was well within the weight limits. It performed very nicely. But the tubing is really a lot thicker than it looks in the pictures. It's very sturdy construction, so you know it will hold. But the hex screws seem kind of chintzy -- couldn't they use thumb screws or something more accessible? The bottom cross tube is very thick and the picture hides the length of the feet extending out the back of the tube (4" or more).<br><br>Maybe my use wasn't ever intended, but I think with a little industrial design, this would be an awesome alternative to a wall mount. It's adequate now but has potential. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0"
